# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Task: Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture Documentation

## Objective

Generate comprehensive architecture documentation for Terraform's plan/apply pipeline. Your documentation should explain how Terraform executes the plan and apply operations, covering the internal components and their interactions.

## Scope

Your documentation should cover the following architectural components:

1. **Graph Builder System**
   - How the dependency graph is constructed
   - The role of graph transformers in building the execution graph
   - How resources, providers, and modules are represented as graph nodes
   - How dependencies between resources are discovered and encoded as edges

2. **Provider Interface and Lifecycle**
   - How providers are initialized and managed during execution
   - The provider plugin architecture
   - How resource operations are delegated to providers
   - Provider configuration and instance management

3. **State Management**
   - How state is read, modified, and persisted during plan/apply
   - The role of state managers and state synchronization
   - How state snapshots enable concurrent graph evaluation
   - State locking and remote state backends

4. **Execution Flow and Hook System**
   - The overall execution flow from command invocation to completion
   - How graph nodes are evaluated (plan vs apply execution)
   - The walker pattern for graph traversal
   - Hook points for extending Terraform's behavior
   - Dynamic expansion for count/for_each resources

## Requirements

- **Component Responsibilities**: Clearly explain what each major component does
- **Data Flow**: Describe how data flows through the system during plan and apply operations
- **Extension Points**: Identify where the architecture allows for customization or extension
- **Error Handling**: Explain how errors are propagated and handled during execution

## Deliverable

Write your documentation to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format.

Your documentation should be technical and precise, aimed at developers who want to understand Terraform's internal architecture. Include specific details about component interactions, not just high-level descriptions.

## Success Criteria

Your documentation will be evaluated on:
- Coverage of all required architectural topics
- Accurate description of component responsibilities and interactions
- Clear explanation of data flow through the pipeline
- Identification of key extension points in the architecture
- Technical depth appropriate for internal architecture documentation

67-assistanttext-
The documentation has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here's a summary of what was covered:

## Documentation Summary

The document covers all four required architectural areas with technical depth drawn directly from reading the Terraform source:

**1. Graph Builder System**
- The `GraphBuilder` interface and `BasicGraphBuilder` pipeline pattern
- `PlanGraphBuilder` vs `ApplyGraphBuilder` and how they differ (config-driven vs diff-driven)
- Full table of graph transformers in order, with their roles
- How `ReferenceTransformer` discovers dependencies via `GraphNodeReferenceable`/`GraphNodeReferencer` interfaces
- Key concrete node types and the interfaces they implement

**2. Provider Interface and Lifecycle**
- The full `providers.Interface` contract (`GetProviderSchema`, `ReadResource`, `PlanResourceChange`, `ApplyResourceChange`, etc.)
- gRPC-based plugin architecture (tfplugin5/6)
- Provider initialization flow through `contextPlugins` factories → `BuiltinEvalContext.InitProvider` → `ConfigureProvider`
- Provider caching, stop propagation, and clean shutdown via `CloseProviderTransformer`

**3. State Management**
- `states.State` data structure hierarchy (State → Module → Resource → ResourceInstance)
- `SyncState` wrapper with `sync.RWMutex` for concurrent graph walk access
- Three-state walk design (`State`, `RefreshState`, `PrevRunState`) with deep copy isolation
- `statemgr.Full` interface for remote backends, locking, and persistence

**4. Execution Flow and Hook System**
- Full plan and apply flows from `Context.PlanAndEval`/`ApplyAndEval` through `planWalk`/walk
- Walker pattern: DAG topological traversal with goroutine parallelism controlled by a semaphore
- Dynamic expansion for count/for_each (two-phase: static expand node → `DynamicExpand` 
... (truncated)

This is intended\\n48: \\t// to avoid redundant re-fetching of schemas when the caller has already\\n49: \\t// loaded them for some other reason.\\n50: \\t//\\n51: \\t// The preloaded schemas do not need to be exhaustive. Terraform will\\n52: \\t// use a preloaded schema if available, or will load a schema directly from\\n53: \\t// a provider if no preloaded schema is available.\\n54: \\t//\\n55: \\t// The caller MUST ensure that the given schemas exactly match those that\\n56: \\t// would be returned from a running provider of the given type or else the\\n57: \\t// runtime behavior is likely to be erratic.\\n58: \\t//\\n59: \\t// Callers must not access (read or write) the given map once it has\\n60: \\t// been passed to Terraform Core using this field.\\n61: \\tPreloadedProviderSchemas map[addrs.Provider]providers.ProviderSchema\\n62: \\n63: \\tUIInput UIInput\\n64: }\\n65: \\n66: // ContextMeta is metadata about the running context. This must be provided by the Context\\n69: // initializer.\\n70: type ContextMeta struct {\\n71: \\tEnv string // Env is the state environment\\n72: \\n73: \\t// OriginalWorkingDir is the working directory where the Terraform CLI\\n74: \\t// was run from, which may no longer actually be the current working\\n75: \\t// directory if the user included the -chdir=... option.\\n76: \\t//\\n77: \\t// If this string is empty then the original working directory is the same\\n78: \\t// as the current working directory.\\n79: \\t//\\n80: \\t// In most cases we should respect the user's override by ignoring this\\n81: \\t// path and just using the current working directory, but this is here\\n82: \\t// for some exceptional cases where the original working directory is\\n83: \\t// needed.\\n84: \\tOriginalWorkingDir string\\n85: }\\n86: \\n87: // Context represents all the context that Terraform needs in order to\\n88: // perform operations on infrastructure. This structure is built using\\n89: // NewContext.\\n90: type Context struct {\\n91: \\t// meta captures some misc. information about the working directory where\\n92: \\t// we're taking these actions, and thus which should remain steady between\\n93: \\t// operations.\\n94: \\tmeta *ContextMeta\\n95: \\n96: \\tplugins *contextPlugins\\n97: \\n98: \\thooks     []Hook\\n99: \\tsh        *stopHook\\n100: \\tuiInput   UIInput\\n101: \\tgraphOpts *ContextGraphOpts\\n102: \\n103: \\tl                   sync.Mutex // Lock acquired during any task\\n104: \\tparallelSem         Semaphore\\n105: \\tproviderInputConfig map[string]map[string]cty.Value\\n106: \\trunCond             *sync.Cond\\n107: \\trunContext          context.Context\\n108: \\trunContextCancel    context.CancelFunc\\n109: }\\n110: \\n111: // (additional methods on Context can be found in context_*.go files.)\\n112: \\n113: // NewContext creates a new Context structure.\\n114: //\\n115: // Once a Context is created, the caller must not access or mutate any of\\n116: // the objects referenced (directly or indirectly) by the ContextOpts fields.\\n117: //\\n118: // If the returned diagnostics contains errors then the resulting context is\\n119: // invalid and must not be used.\\n120: func NewContext(opts *ContextOpts) (*Context, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\\n121: \\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\\n122: \\n123: \\tlog.Printf(\\\"[TRACE] terraform.NewContext: starting\\\")\\n124: \\n125: \\t// Copy all the hooks and add our stop hook. We do this both to limit\\n133: \\t// CPU pressure but also to have an extra guard against rate throttling\\n134: \\t// from providers.\\n135: \\t// We throw an error in case of negative parallelism\\n136: \\tpar := opts.Parallelism\\n137: \\tif par < 0 {\\n138: \\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\\n139: \\t\\t\\ttfdiags.Error,\\n140: \\t\\t\\t\\\"Invalid parallelism value\\\",\\n141: \\t\\t\\tfmt.Sprintf(\\\"The parallelism must be a positive value. \\n188: type ContextGraphOpts struct {\\n189: \\t// If false, skip the graph structure validation.\\n190: \\tSkipGraphValidation bool\\n191: \\n192: \\t// Legacy graphs only: won't prune the graph\\n193: \\tVerbose bool\\n194: }\\n195: \\n196: // Stop stops the running task.\\n197: //\\n198: // Stop will block until the task completes.\\n199: func (c *Context) Stop() {\\n200: \\tlog.Printf(\\\"[WARN] terraform: Stop called, initiating interrupt sequence\\\")\\n201: \\n202: \\tc.l.Lock()\\n203: \\tdefer c.l.Unlock()\\n204: \\n205: \\t// If we're running, then stop\\n206: \\t}\\n228: \\n229: \\tlog.Printf(\\\"[WARN] terraform: stop complete\\\")\\n230: }\\n231: \\n232: func (c *Context) acquireRun(phase string) func() {\\n233: \\t// With the run lock held, grab the \\n255: func (c *Context) releaseRun() {\\n256: \\t// Grab the context lock so that we can make modifications to fields\\n257: \\tc.l.Lock()\\n258: \\tdefer c.l.Unlock()\\n259: \\n260: \\t// End our When the watch is no longer needed, the\\n278: // `stop` chan should be closed before waiting on the `wait` chan.\\n279: // The `wait` chan is important, because without synchronizing with the end of\\n280: // the watchStop goroutine, the runContext may also be closed during the select\\n281: // incorrectly causing providers to be stopped. \\n306: \\t\\t// If we're here, we're stopped, trigger the call.\\n307: \\t\\tlog.Printf(\\\"[TRACE] Context: requesting providers and provisioners to gracefully stop\\\")\\n308: \\n309: \\t\\t{\\n310: \\t\\t\\t// Copy the providers so that a misbehaved blocking Stop doesn't\\n311: \\t\\t\\t// completely hang Terraform.\\n312: \\t\\t\\twalker.providerLock.Lock()\\n313: \\t\\t\\tps := \\t\\t}\\n343: \\t}()\\n344: \\n345: \\treturn stop, wait\\n346: }\\n347: \\n348: func (c *Context) checkStateDependencies(state *states.State) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\\n349: \\tif state == nil {\\n350:     "content": "1: // Copyright (c) HashiCorp, Inc.\n2: // SPDX-License-Identifier: BUSL-1.1\n3: \n4: package terraform\n5: \n6: import (\n7: \t\"context\"\n8: \t\"fmt\"\n9: \t\"log\"\n10: \t\"sort\"\n11: \t\"sync\"\n12: \n13: \t\"github.com/zclconf/go-cty/cty\"\n14: \n15: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/addrs\"\n16: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/configs\"\n17: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/logging\"\n18: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/providers\"\n19: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/provisioners\"\n20: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/states\"\n21: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/tfdiags\"\n22: )\n23: \n24: // InputMode defines what sort of input will be asked for when Input\n25: // is called on Context.\n26: type InputMode byte\n27: \n28: const (\n29: \t// InputModeProvider asks for provider variables\n30: \tInputModeProvider InputMode = 1 << iota\n31: \n32: \t// InputModeStd is the standard operating mode and asks for both variables\n33: \t// and providers.\n34: \tInputModeStd = InputModeProvider\n35: )\n36: \n37: // ContextOpts are the user-configurable options to create a context with\n38: // NewContext.\n39: type ContextOpts struct {\n40: \tMeta         *ContextMeta\n41: \tHooks        []Hook\n42: \tParallelism  int\n43: \tProviders    map[addrs.Provider]providers.Factory\n44: \tProvisioners map[string]provisioners.Factory\n45: \n46: \t// PreloadedProviderSchemas is an optional map of provider schemas that\n47: \t// were already loaded from providers by the caller. This is intended\n48: \t// to avoid redundant re-fetching of schemas when the caller has already\n49: \t// loaded them for some other reason.\n50: \t//\n51: \t// The preloaded schemas do not need to be exhaustive. Terraform will\n52: \t// use a preloaded schema if available, or will load a schema directly from\n53: \t// a provider if no preloaded schema is available.\n54: \t//\n55: \t// The caller MUST ensure that the given schemas exactly match those that\n56: \t// would be returned from a running provider of the given type or else the\n57: \t// runtime behavior is likely to be erratic.\n58: \t//\n59: \t// Callers must not access (read or write) the given map once it has\n60: \t// been passed to Terraform Core using this field.\n61: \tPreloadedProviderSchemas map[addrs.Provider]providers.ProviderSchema\n62: \n63: \tUIInput UIInput\n64: }\n65: \n66: // ContextMeta is metadata about the running context.     "content": "1: // Copyright (c) HashiCorp, Inc.\n2: // SPDX-License-Identifier: BUSL-1.1\n3: \n4: package terraform\n5: \n6: import (\n7: \t\"log\"\n8: \n9: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/addrs\"\n10: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/configs\"\n11: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/dag\"\n12: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/moduletest/mocking\"\n13: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/providers\"\n14: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/states\"\n15: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/tfdiags\"\n16: )\n17: \n18: // PlanGraphBuilder is a GraphBuilder implementation that builds a graph for\n19: // planning and for other \"plan-like\" operations which don't require an\n20: // already-calculated plan as input.\n21: //\n22: // Unlike the apply graph builder, this graph builder:\n23: //\n24: //   - Makes its decisions primarily based on the given configuration, which\n25: //     represents the desired state.\n26: //\n27: //   - Ignores certain lifecycle concerns like create_before_destroy, because\n28: //     those are only important once we already know what action we're planning\n29: //     to take against a particular resource instance.\n30: type PlanGraphBuilder struct {\n31: \t// Config is the configuration tree to build a plan from.\n32: \tConfig *configs.Config\n33: \n34: \t// State is the current state\n35: \tState *states.State\n36: \n37: \t// RootVariableValues are the raw input values for root input variables\n38: \t// given by the caller, which we'll resolve into final values as part\n39: \t// of the plan walk.\n40: \tRootVariableValues InputValues\n41: \n42: \t// ExternalProviderConfigs are pre-initialized root module provider\n43: \t// configurations that the graph builder should assume will be available\n44: \t// immediately during the subsequent plan walk, without any explicit\n45: \t// initialization step.\n46: \tExternalProviderConfigs map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n47: \n48: \t// Plugins is a library of plug-in components (providers and\n49: \t// provisioners) available for use.\n50: \tPlugins *contextPlugins\n51: \n52: \t// Targets are resources to target\n53: \tTargets []addrs.Targetable\n54: \n55: \t// ActionTargets are actions that should be triggered.\n56: \tActionTargets []addrs.Targetable\n57: \n58: \t// ForceReplace are resource instances where if we would normally have\n59: \t// generated a NoOp or Update action then we'll force generating a replace\n60: \t// action instead. Create and Delete actions are not affected.\n61: \tForceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n62: \n63: \t// skipRefresh indicates that we should skip refreshing managed resources\n64: \tskipRefresh bool\n65: \n66: \t// preDestroyRefresh indicates that we are executing the refresh which\n67: \t// happens immediately before a destroy plan, which happens to use the\n68: \t// normal planing mode so skipPlanChanges cannot be set.\n69: \tpreDestroyRefresh bool\n70: \n71: \t// skipPlanChanges indicates that we should skip the step of comparing\n72: \t// prior state with configuration and generating planned changes to\n73: \t// resource instances. (This is for the \"refresh only\" planning mode,\n74: \t// where we _only_ do the refresh step.)\n75: \tskipPlanChanges bool\n76: \n77: \tConcreteProvider                ConcreteProviderNodeFunc\n78: \tConcreteResource                ConcreteResourceNodeFunc\n79: \tConcreteResourceInstance        ConcreteResourceInstanceNodeFunc\n80: \tConcreteResourceOrphan          ConcreteResourceInstanceNodeFunc\n81: \tConcreteResourceInstanceDeposed ConcreteResourceInstanceDeposedNodeFunc\n82: \tConcreteModule                  ConcreteModuleNodeFunc\n83: \t// ConcreteAction is only used by the ConfigTransformer during the Validate\n84: \t// Graph walk; otherwise we fall back to the DefaultConcreteActionFunc.\n85: \tConcreteAction ConcreteActionNodeFunc\n86: \n87: \t// Plan Operation this graph will be used for.\n88: \tOperation walkOperation\n89: \n90: \t// ExternalReferences allows the external caller to pass in references to\n91: \t// nodes that should not be pruned even if they are not referenced within\n92: \t// the actual graph.\n93: \tExternalReferences []*addrs.Reference\n94: \n95: \t// Overrides provides the set of overrides supplied by the testing\n96: \t// framework.\n97: \tOverrides *mocking.Overrides\n98: \n99: \t// ImportTargets are the list of resources to import.\n100: \tImportTargets []*ImportTarget\n101: \n102: \t// forgetResources lists the resources that are to be forgotten, i.e. removed\n103: \t// from state without destroying.\n104: \tforgetResources []addrs.ConfigResource\n105: \n106: \t// forgetModules lists the modules that are to be forgotten, i.e. removed\n107: \t// from state without destroying.\n108: \tforgetModules []addrs.Module\n109: \n110: \t// GenerateConfig tells Terraform where to write and generated config for\n111: \t// any import targets that do not already have configuration.\n112: \t//\n113: \t// If empty, then config will not be generated.\n114: \tGenerateConfigPath string\n115: \n116: \t// SkipGraphValidation indicates whether the graph builder should skip\n117: \t// validation of the graph.\n118: \tSkipGraphValidation bool\n119: \n120: \t// If true, the graph builder will generate a query plan instead of a\n121: \t// normal plan. This is used for the \"terraform query\" command.\n122: \tqueryPlan bool\n123: \n124: \t// overridePreventDestroy is only applicable during destroy operations, and\n125: \t// allows Terraform to ignore the configuration attribute prevent_destroy\n126: \t// to destroy resources regardless.\n127: \toverridePreventDestroy bool\n128: \n129: \t// AllowRootEphemeralOutputs overrides a specific check made within the\n130: \t// output nodes that they cannot be ephemeral at within root modules. This\n131: \t// should be set to true for plans executing from within either the stacks\n132: \t// or test runtimes, where the root modules as Terraform sees them aren't\n133: \t// the actual root modules.\n134: \tAllowRootEphemeralOutputs bool\n135: }\n136: \n137: // See GraphBuilder\n138: func (b *PlanGraphBuilder) Build(path addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n139: b.Operation == walkPlanDestroy,\n215: \t\t\tOverrides:                 b.Overrides,\n216: \t\t\tAllowRootEphemeralOutputs: b.AllowRootEphemeralOutputs,\n217: \n218: \t\t\t// NOTE: We currently treat Check block data\n227: \t\t// sources were added earlier.\n228: \t\t&checkTransformer{\n229: \t\t\tConfig:    b.Config,\n230: \t\t\tOperation: b.Operation,\n231: \t\t},\n232: \n233: \t\t// Add orphan resources\n234: \t\t&OrphanResourceInstanceTransformer{\n235: \t\t\tConcrete: b.ConcreteResourceOrphan,\n236: \t\t\tState:    b.State,\n237: \t\t\tConfig:   b.Config,\n238: \t\t\tskip:     b.Operation == walkPlanDestroy,\n239: \t\t},\n240: \n241: \t\t// We also need nodes for any deposed instance objects present in the\n242: \t\t// state, so we can plan to destroy them. Terraform to exit\n133: \t// ASAP and in that case it's possible that if Terraform runs for too much\n134: \t// longer then it'll get killed un-gracefully, and so this hook could be\n135: \t// an The refreshing operation during destroy must be a special case,\n48: \t// which can allow for missing instances in the state, and avoid blocking\n49: \t// on failing condition tests. The destroy plan itself should be\n50: \t// responsible for this special case of refreshing, and the separate\n51: \t// pre-destroy plan removed entirely.\n52: \tPreDestroyRefresh bool\n53: \n54: \t// SetVariables are the raw values for root module variables as provided\n55: \t// by the user who is requesting the run, prior to any normalization or\n56: \t// substitution of defaults. See the documentation for the InputValue\n57: \t// type for more information on how to correctly populate this.\n58: \tSetVariables InputValues\n59: \n60: \t// If Targets has a non-zero length then it activates targeted planning\n61: \t// mode, where Terraform will take actions only for resource instances\n62: \t// mentioned in this set and any other objects those resource instances\n63: \t// depend on.\n64: \t//\n65: \t// Targeted planning mode is intended for exceptional use only,\n66: \t// and so populating this field will cause Terraform to generate extra\n67: \t// warnings as part of the planning result.\n68: \tTargets []addrs.Targetable\n69: \n70: \t// ActionTargets represents the actions that should be triggered by this\n71: \t// execution. This is incompatible with the `Targets` attribute, only one\n72: \t// can be set. Also, Mode must be plans.RefreshOnly when using\n73: \t// ActionTargets.\n74: \t//\n75: \t// TEMP: For now, only support a single entry in this slice.\n76: \tActionTargets []addrs.Targetable\n77: \n78: \t// ForceReplace is a set of resource instance addresses whose corresponding\n79: \t// objects should be forced planned for replacement if the provider's\n80: \t// plan would otherwise have been to either update the object in-place or\n81: \t// to take no action on it at all.\n82: \t//\n83: \t// A typical use of this argument is to ask Terraform to replace an object\n84: \t// which the user has determined is somehow degraded (via information from\n85: \t// outside of Terraform), thereby hopefully replacing it with a\n86: \t// fully-functional new object.\n87: \tForceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n88: \n89: \t// DeferralAllowed specifies that the plan is allowed to defer some actions,\n90: \t// so that a subset of the plan can be applied even if parts of it can't yet\n91: \t// be planned at all. Plans that contain deferred actions can't converge in\n92: \t// a single run, and their configuration must be planned again after the\n93: \t// dependencies of their deferred objects are in a usable state. Various\n94: \t// events can cause deferrals, including unknown values in count and\n95: \t// for_each arguments, and deferral notices from providers. If\n96: \t// DeferralAllowed is false, the plan will error upon encountering an object\n97: \t// that would be unplannable until after the apply.\n98: \tDeferralAllowed bool\n99: \n100: \t// ExternalReferences allows the external caller to pass in references to\n101: \t// nodes that should not be pruned even if they are not referenced within\n102: \t// the actual graph.\n103: \tExternalReferences []*addrs.Reference\n104: \n105: \t// ExternalDependencyDeferred, when set, indicates that the caller\n106: \t// considers this configuration to depend on some other configuration\n107: \t// that had at least one deferred change, and therefore everything in\n108: \t// this configuration must have its changes deferred too so that the\n109: \t// overall dependency ordering would be correct.\n110: \tExternalDependencyDeferred bool\n111: \n112: \t// Overrides provides a set of override objects that should be applied\n113: \t// during this plan.\n114: \tOverrides *mocking.Overrides\n115: \n116: \t// GenerateConfigPath tells Terraform where to write any generated\n117: \t// configuration for any ImportTargets that do not have configuration\n118: \t// already.\n119: \t//\n120: \t// If empty, then no config will be generated.\n121: \tGenerateConfigPath string\n122: \n123: \t// ExternalProviders are clients for pre-configured providers that are\n124: \t// treated as being passed into the root module from the caller. This\n125: \t// is equivalent to writing a \"providers\" argument inside a \"module\"\n126: \t// block in the Terraform language, but for the root module the caller\n127: \t// is written in Go rather than the Terraform language.\n128: \t//\n129: \t// Terraform Core will NOT call ValidateProviderConfig or ConfigureProvider\n130: \t// on any providers in this map; it's the caller's responsibility to\n131: \t// configure these providers based on information outside the scope of\n132: \t// the root module.\n133: \tExternalProviders map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n134: \n135: \t// ForcePlanTimestamp, if not nil, will force the \"plantimestamp\" function\n136: \t// to return the given value instead of the time when the plan operation\n137: \t// started.\n138: \t//\n139: \t// This is here only to allow producing fixed results for tests. Don't\n140: \t// use it for main code.\n141: \tForcePlanTimestamp *time.Time\n142: \n143: \t// Forget if set to true will cause the plan to forget all resources. This can only be set during a destroy plan, and should\n154: \t// only be set during the test command.\n155: \tOverridePreventDestroy bool\n156: \n157: \t// AllowRootEphemeralOutputs overrides a specific check made within the\n158: \t// output nodes that they cannot be ephemeral at within root modules. This\n159: \t// should be set to true for plans executing from within either the stacks\n160: \t// or test runtimes, where the root modules as Terraform sees them aren't\n161: \t// the actual root modules.\n162: \tAllowRootEphemeralOutputs bool\n163: }\n164: \n165: // Plan generates an execution plan by comparing the given configuration\n166: // with the given previous run state.\n167: //\n168: // The given planning options allow control of various other details of the\n169: // planning process that are not represented directly in the configuration.\n170: // You can use terraform.DefaultPlanOpts to generate a normal plan with no\n171: // special options.\n172: //\n173: // If the returned diagnostics contains no errors then the returned plan is\n174: // applyable, although Terraform cannot guarantee that applying it will fully\n175: // succeed. If the returned diagnostics contains errors but this method\n176: // still returns a non-nil Plan then the plan describes the subset of actions\n177: // planned so far, which is not safe to apply but could potentially be used\n178: // by the UI layer to give extra context to support understanding of the\n179: // returned error messages.\n180: func (c *Context) Plan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n181: \tplan, _, diags := c.PlanAndEval(config, prevRunState, opts)\n182: \treturn plan, diags\n183: }\n184: \n185: // PlanAndEval is like [Context.Plan] except that it additionally makes a\n186: // best effort to return a [lang.Scope] which can evaluate expressions in the\n187: // root module based on the content of the generated plan.\n188: //\n189: // The scope will be nil if the planning process doesn't complete successfully\n190: // enough to produce a valid evaluation scope. For\n471: // handling real user requests to run Terraform, it'd probably be better\n472: // to construct a *PlanOpts value directly and provide a way for the user\n473: // to set values for all of its fields.\n474: //\n475: // The \"mode\" and \"setVariables\" arguments become the values of the \"Mode\"\n476: // and \"SetVariables\" fields in the result. }\n496: \n497: func (c *Context) refreshOnlyPlan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n498: \tvar diags This is required because\n552: \t// a \"destroy plan\" is only creating delete changes, and is essentially a\n553: \t// local operation.\n554: \t//\n555: \t// NOTE: if skipRefresh _is_ set then we'll rely on the destroy-plan walk\n556: \t// below to upgrade the prevRunState and priorState both to the latest\n557: \t// resource type schemas, so NodePlanDestroyableResourceInstance.Execute\n558: \t// must coordinate with this by taking that action only when c.skipRefresh\n559: \t// _is_ set. This coupling between the two is unfortunate but necessary\n560: \t// to work within our current structure.\n561: \tif !opts.SkipRefresh && !prevRunState.Empty() {\n562: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Context.destroyPlan: calling Context.plan to get the effect of refreshing the prior state\")\n563: \t\trefreshOpts := *opts\n564: \t\trefreshOpts.Mode = plans.NormalMode\n565: \t\trefreshOpts.PreDestroyRefresh = true\n566: \t\trefreshOpts.OverridePreventDestroy = false\n567: \n568: \t\t// FIXME: A normal plan is required here to refresh the state, because\n569: \t\t// the state and configuration may not match during a destroy, and a\n570: \t\t// normal refresh plan can fail with evaluation errors. In the future\n571: \t\t// the destroy plan should take care of refreshing instances itself,\n572: \t\t// where the special cases of evaluation and skipping condition checks\n573: \t\t// can be whether\n577: \t\t\t// there are errors, just in case there are warnings we'd want to\n578: \t\t\t// preserve, but we're intentionally _not_ doing that here because\n579: \t\t\t// if the first plan succeeded then we'll be running another plan\n580: \t\t\t// in DestroyMode below, and we don't want to double-up any\n581: \t\t\t// warnings that both plan walks would generate.\n582: \t\t\t// (This does mean we won't show any warnings that would've been\n583: \t\t\t// unique to only this walk, but we're assuming here that if the\n584: \t\t\t// warnings aren't also applicable to a destroy plan then we'd\n585: \t\t\t// rather not show them here, because this non-destroy plan for\n586: \t\t\t// refreshing is largely an implementation detail.)\n587: \t\t\tdiags = diags\n625: }\n626: \n627: func (c *Context) prePlanFindAndApplyMoves(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State) ([]refactoring.MoveStatement, refactoring.MoveResults, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n628: \texplicitMoveStmts := refactoring.FindMoveStatements(config)\n629: \timplicitMoveStmts := refactoring.ImpliedMoveStatements(config, prevRunState, explicitMoveStmts)\n630: \tvar moveStmts []addrs.Targetable) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n641: \tif len(targets) < 1 {\n642: \t\treturn nil // the following only matters when targeting\n643: \t}\n644: \n645: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n646: \n647: \tvar excluded []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n648: \tfor _, result := range moveResults.Changes.Values() {\n649: \t\tfromMatchesTarget := false\n650: \t\ttoMatchesTarget := false\n651: \t\tfor _, targetAddr := range targets {\n652: \t\t\tif targetAddr.TargetContains(result.From) {\n653: \t\t\t\tfromMatchesTarget = true\n654: \t\t\t}\n655: \t\t\tif targetAddr.TargetContains(result.To) {\n656: \t\t\t\ttoMatchesTarget = true\n657: \t\t\t}\n658: \t\t}\n659: \t\tif !fromMatchesTarget {\n660: \t\t\texcluded = append(excluded, result.From)\n661: \t\t}\n662: \t\tif !toMatchesTarget {\n663: \t\t\texcluded = append(excluded, result.To)\n664: \t\t}\n665: \t}\n666: \tif len(excluded) > 0 {\n667: \t\tsort.Slice(excluded, func(i, j int) bool {\n668: \t\t\treturn excluded[i].Less(excluded[j])\n669: \t\t})\n670: \n671: \t\tvar listBuf strings.Builder\n672: \t\tvar prevResourceAddr addrs.AbsResource\n673: \t\tfor _, instAddr := range excluded {\n674: \t\t\t// Targeting generally ends up selecting whole resources rather\n675: \t\t\t// than individual instances, because we don't factor in\n676: \t\t\t// individual instances until DynamicExpand, so we're going to\n677: \t\t\t// always show whole resource addresses here, excluding any\n678: \t\t\t// instance keys. (This also neatly avoids dealing with the\n679: \t\t\t// different quoting styles required for string instance keys\n680: \t\t\t// on different shells, which is handy.)\n681: \t\t\t//\n682: \t\t\t// To avoid showing duplicates when we have multiple instances\n683: \t\t\t// of the same resource, we'll remember the most recent\n684: \t\t\t// resource we rendered in prevResource, which is sufficient\n685: \t\t\t// because we sorted the list of instance addresses above, and\n686: \t\t\t// our sort order always groups together instances of the same\n687: \t\t\t// resource.\n688: \t\t\tresourceAddr := instAddr.ContainingResource()\n689: \t\t\tif resourceAddr.Equal(prevResourceAddr) {\n690: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n691: \t\t\t}\n692: \t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&listBuf, \"\\n  -target=%q\", resourceAddr.String())\n693: \t\t\tprevResourceAddr = resourceAddr\n694: \t\t}\n695: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n696: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n697: \t\t\t\"Moved resource instances excluded by targeting\",\n698: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n699: \t\t\t\t\"Resource instances in your current state have moved to new addresses in the latest configuration. Terraform must include those resource instances while planning in order to ensure a correct result, but your -target=... options do not fully cover all of those resource instances.\\n\\nTo create a valid plan, either remove your -target=... options altogether or add the following additional target options:%s\\n\\nNote that adding these options may include further additional resource instances in your plan, in order to respect object dependencies.\",\n700: \t\t\t\tlistBuf.String(),\n701: \t\t\t),\n702: \t\t))\n703: \t}\n704: \n705: \treturn diags\n706: }\n707: \n708: func (c *Context) }\n711: \n712: // findImportTargets builds a list of import targets from any import blocks in\n713: // config.\n714: func (c *Context) findImportTargets(config *configs.Config) []*ImportTarget {\n715:         prevRunState,\n796: \t\tExternalProviderConfigs:    externalProviderConfigs,\n797: \t\tDeferralAllowed:            opts.DeferralAllowed,\n798: \t\tExternalDependencyDeferred: This oddity\n816: \t\t// comes from the fact that we need to apply the moves before we\n817: \t\t// actually validate them, because validation depends on the result\n818: \t\t// of first trying to plan.\n819: \t\treturn nil, nil, moveValidateDiags\n820: \t}\n821: \tdiags = diags.Append(moveValidateDiags) // might just contain warnings\n822: \n823: \tif moveResults.Blocked.Len() > 0 && !diags.HasErrors() {\n824: \t\t// If we had blocked moves and we're not going to be returning errors\n825: \t\t// then we'll report the blockers as a warning. This is here mainly for convenient internal use such\n59: // as in test cases.\n60: func (po *PlanOpts) ApplyOpts() *ApplyOpts {\n61: \treturn &ApplyOpts{\n62: \t\tExternalProviders:         po.ExternalProviders,\n63: \t\tAllowRootEphemeralOutputs: po.AllowRootEphemeralOutputs,\n64: \t}\n65: }\n66: \n67: // Apply performs the actions described by the given Plan object and returns\n68: // the resulting updated state.\n69: //\n70: // The given configuration *must* be the same configuration that was passed\n71: // earlier to Context.Plan in order to create this plan.\n72: //\n73: // Even if the returned diagnostics contains errors, Apply always returns the\n74: // resulting state which is likely to have been partially-updated.\n75: //\n76: // The [opts] argument may be nil to indicate that no special options are\n77: // required. Some\n78: // options in [PlanOpts] when creating a plan must be echoed with equivalent\n79: // settings during apply, so leaving opts as nil might not be valid for\n80: // certain combinations of plan-time options.\n81: func (c *Context) Apply(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts) (*states.State, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n82: \tstate, _, diags := c.ApplyAndEval(plan, config, opts)\n83: \treturn state, diags\n84: }\n85: \n86: // ApplyAndEval is like [Context.Apply] except that it additionally makes a\n87: // best effort to return a [lang.Scope] which can evaluate expressions in the\n88: // root module based on the content of the new state.\n89: //\n90: // The scope will be nil if the apply process doesn't complete successfully\n91: // enough to produce a valid evaluation scope. We'll\n126: \t\t\t// reject it on the assumption that something very strange is\n127: \t\t\t// going on. and so better to halt than do something incorrect.\n128: \t\t\t// This error message is generic and useless because we don't\n129: \t\t\t// expect anyone to ever see it in normal use.\n130: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n131: \t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n132: \t\t\t\t\"Cannot apply non-applyable plan\",\n133: \t\t\t\t`The given plan is not applyable. If this seems like a bug in Terraform, then please report it!`,\n134: \t\t\t))\n135: \t\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n136: \t\t}\n137: \t}\n138: \n139: \t// The caller must provide values for all of the \"apply-time variables\"\n140: \t// mentioned in the plan, and for no others because the others come from\n141: \t// the plan itself.\n142: \tdiags = diags.Append(checkApplyTimeVariables(plan.ApplyTimeVariables, opts.SetVariables, config))\n143: \n144: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n145: \t\t// If the apply request is invalid in some way then we'll bail out\n146: \t\t// here before we do any real work.\n147: \t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n148: \t}\n149: \n150: \tfor _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {\n151: \t\t// Import is a no-op change during an apply (all the real action happens during the plan) but we'd\n152: \t\t// like to show some helpful output that mirrors the way we show other changes.\n153: \t\tif rc.Importing != nil {\n154: \t\t\thookResourceID := HookResourceIdentity{\n155: \t\t\t\tAddr:         rc.Addr,\n156: \t\t\t\tProviderAddr: rc.ProviderAddr.Provider,\n157: \t\t\t}\n158: \t\t\tfor _, h := range c.hooks {\n159: \t\t\t\t// In future, we may need to call PostApplyImport separately elsewhere in the apply\n160: \t\t\t\t// operation. To stop this, we'll catch the panic log\\n57: \\t\\t\\t\\t// that the vertex panicked without finishing and re-panic.\\n58: \\t\\t\\t\\tlog.Printf(\\\"[ERROR] vertex %q panicked\\\", dag.VertexName(v))\\n59: \\t\\t\\t\\tpanic(r) // re-panic\\n60: \\t\\t\\t}\\n61: \\n62: \\t\\t\\tif diags.HasErrors() {\\n63: \\t\\t\\t\\tfor _, diag := range diags {\\n64: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tif diag.Severity() == tfdiags.Error {\\n65: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\tdesc := diag.Description()\\n66: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\tlog.Printf(\\\"[ERROR] vertex %q error: %s\\\", dag.VertexName(v), desc.Summary)\\n67: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n68: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n69: \\t\\t\\t\\tlog.Printf(\\\"[TRACE] vertex %q: visit complete, with errors\\\", dag.VertexName(v))\\n70: \\t\\t\\t} else {\\n71: \\t\\t\\t\\tlog.Printf(\\\"[TRACE] vertex %q: visit complete\\\", dag.VertexName(v))\\n72: \\t\\t\\t}\\n73: \\t\\t}()\\n74: \\n75: \\t\\thaveOverrides := !ctx.Overrides().Empty()\\n76: \\n77: \\t\\t// If the graph node is overridable, we'll check our overrides to see\\n78: \\t\\t// if we need to apply any overrides to the node.\\n79: \\t\\tif overridable, ok := v.(GraphNodeOverridable); ok && haveOverrides {\\n80: \\t\\t\\t// It'd be nice if we could just pass the overrides directly into\\n81: \\t\\t\\t// the nodes, but the way the AbstractNodeResource is created is\\n82: \\t\\t\\t// complicated and it's not easy to make sure that every\\n83: \\t\\t\\t// implementation sets the overrides correctly. Instead, we just\\n84: \\t\\t\\t// do it from this single location to keep things simple.\\n85: \\t\\t\\t//\\n86: \\t\\t\\t// See the output node for an example of providing the overrides\\n87: \\t\\t\\t// directly to the node.\\n88: \\t\\t\\tif override, ok := ctx.Overrides().GetResourceOverride(overridable.ResourceInstanceAddr(), overridable.ConfigProvider()); ok {\\n89: \\t\\t\\t\\toverridable.SetOverride(override)\\n90: \\t\\t\\t}\\n91: \\t\\t}\\n92: \\n93: \\t\\tif provider, ok := v.(GraphNodeProvider); ok && haveOverrides {\\n94: \\t\\t\\t// If we find a legacy provider within an overridden module, we\\n95: \\t\\t\\t// can't evaluate the config so we have to skip it. We do this here\\n96: \\t\\t\\t// for the similar reasons as the resource overrides above, and to\\n97: \\t\\t\\t// keep all the override logic together.\\n98: \\t\\t\\taddr := provider.ProviderAddr()\\n99: \\t\\t\\t// UnkeyedInstanceShim is used by legacy provider configs within a\\n100: \\t\\t\\t// module to return an instance of that module, since they can never\\n101: \\t\\t\\t// exist within an expanded instance.\\n102: \\t\\t\\tif ctx.Overrides().IsOverridden(addr.Module.UnkeyedInstanceShim()) {\\n103: \\t\\t\\t\\tlog.Printf(\\\"[DEBUG] skipping provider %s found within overridden module\\\", addr)\\n104: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn\\n105: \\t\\t\\t}\\n106: \\t\\t}\\n107: \\n108: \\t\\t// vertexCtx is the context that we use when evaluating. This\\n109: \\t\\t// is normally the global context but can be overridden\\n110: \\t\\t// with either a GraphNodeModuleInstance, GraphNodePartialExpandedModule,\\n111: \\t\\t// or graphNodeEvalContextScope implementation. 30. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline: Internal Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform's plan/apply pipeline is the core engine responsible for computing the difference between desired infrastructure state (expressed in configuration) and actual state (tracked in state files), and then applying the necessary changes. The pipeline is implemented in `internal/terraform/` and structured around four interacting systems: the **Graph Builder**, the **Provider Interface**, **State Management**, and the **Execution Flow with Hook System**.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Graph Builder System\n\n### The `GraphBuilder` Interface\n\nThe central abstraction for all graph construction is the `GraphBuilder` interface (`internal/terraform/graph_builder.go`):\n\n```go\ntype GraphBuilder interface {\n    Build(addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n}\n```\n\nThe `BasicGraphBuilder` is the universal implementation. It holds an ordered list of `GraphTransformer` steps and executes them sequentially, each transformer receiving and mutating the growing graph:\n\n```go\ntype BasicGraphBuilder struct {\n    Steps               []GraphTransformer\n    Name                string\n    SkipGraphValidation bool\n}\n```\n\nEach step calls `step.Transform(g)`, which may add nodes, add edges, prune nodes, or reorganize the graph. After all steps complete, the graph is optionally validated for acyclicity.\n\n### Operation-Specific Graph Builders\n\nTwo concrete builders correspond to the two main operations:\n\n**`PlanGraphBuilder`** (`internal/terraform/graph_builder_plan.go`): Builds the graph for `terraform plan`. It uses configuration as its primary input and is aware of the current state for orphan detection. It supports multiple plan operations (`walkPlan`, `walkPlanDestroy`, `walkValidate`, `walkImport`), each initialized with different concrete node types through factory functions (`ConcreteProvider`, `ConcreteResource`, etc.).\n\n**`ApplyGraphBuilder`** (`internal/terraform/graph_builder_apply.go`): Builds the graph for `terraform apply`. It derives its structure from the _plan's change set_ (`plans.ChangesSrc`) rather than the configuration directly, ensuring apply only touches resources explicitly planned. It uses the `DiffTransformer` to create nodes from planned changes.\n\n### Graph Transformers\n\nGraph transformers are the building blocks of graph construction. Each implements:\n\n```go\ntype GraphTransformer interface {\n    Transform(*Graph) error\n}\n```\n\nThe ordered transformer pipeline in both builders includes (in roughly this sequence):\n\n| Transformer | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `ConfigTransformer` | Creates nodes for all resources declared in config |\n| `StateTransformer` | Creates nodes for resources present in state (for deposed/orphan handling) |\n| `OrphanResourceInstanceTransformer` | Adds nodes for resources in state but removed from config |\n| `AttachStateTransformer` | Attaches state data to nodes that need it |\n| `AttachResourceConfigTransformer` | Attaches HCL config blocks to resource nodes |\n| `transformProviders(...)` | Adds provider nodes and edges connecting them to their resources |\n| `AttachSchemaTransformer` | Loads and attaches provider schemas to all relevant nodes |\n| `ModuleExpansionTransformer` | Creates expansion nodes for module calls using count/for_each |\n| `ReferenceTransformer` | Reads node references and creates dependency edges |\n| `AttachDependenciesTransformer` | Records resolved dependencies on resource nodes |\n| `DestroyEdgeTransformer` | Adds destruction-order edges for replace/destroy actions |\n| `ForcedCBDTransformer` | Detects cycles from create_before_destroy and forces CBD ordering |\n| `TargetsTransformer` | Prunes graph to only targeted resources |\n| `CloseProviderTransformer` | Adds \"close\" nodes after last use of each provider |\n| `CloseRootModuleTransformer` | Adds the terminal root node |\n| `TransitiveReductionTransformer` | Removes redundant edges (keeps graph minimal) |\n\n### How Dependency Edges Are Discovered\n\nThe `ReferenceTransformer` is responsible for dependency edges. It works by calling two interfaces:\n\n- **`GraphNodeReferenceable`**: Implemented by nodes that other nodes can depend on (resources, modules, locals, outputs). Returns referenceable addresses.\n- **`GraphNodeReferencer`**: Implemented by nodes that reference other nodes. Returns a list of `*addrs.Reference` parsed from the node's configuration expressions.\n\nWhen `ReferenceTransformer` runs, it matches each referencer's references against the referenceable addresses in the same module scope and adds a directed edge from the referencer to the dependency. Explicit `depends_on` blocks are treated as additional references.\n\n### Graph Node Types\n\nNodes in the graph implement various combinations of interfaces to declare their roles:\n\n- **`GraphNodeExecutable`**: Has an `Execute(EvalContext, walkOperation)` method called during the walk.\n- **`GraphNodeDynamicExpandable`**: Has a `DynamicExpand(EvalContext)` method that returns a sub-graph (used for count/for_each expansion).\n- **`GraphNodeReferenceable`** / **`GraphNodeReferencer`**: Participate in reference-based dependency edges.\n- **`GraphNodeProvider`**: Represents a provider instance node.\n- **`GraphNodeModuleInstance`**: Belongs to a specific expanded module instance.\n\nKey concrete node types:\n\n| Node Type | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `nodeExpandPlannableResource` | Expand node for a resource during plan; expands to per-instance nodes |\n| `NodePlannableResourceInstance` | Single instance during plan; calls `PlanResourceChange` |\n| `NodeApplyableResourceInstance` | Single instance during apply; calls `ApplyResourceChange` |\n| `NodeApplyableProvider` | Initializes and configures a provider |\n| `nodeExpandModule` | Expands a module call into instances based on count/for_each |\n| `NodeApplyableModuleVariable` | Evaluates a module input variable |\n| `NodeApplyableOutput` | Evaluates and persists an output value |\n\n### The `Graph` Struct\n\nThe `Graph` struct (`internal/terraform/graph.go`) embeds `dag.AcyclicGraph`, which is a directed acyclic graph implementation from `internal/dag`. The graph also carries a `Path` (`addrs.ModuleInstance`) representing the module the graph is rooted in.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Provider Interface and Lifecycle\n\n### The `providers.Interface`\n\nAll provider implementations in Terraform must satisfy the `providers.Interface` (`internal/providers/provider.go`). This is the complete contract between Terraform Core and provider plugins:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    GetProviderSchema() GetProviderSchemaResponse\n    ValidateProviderConfig(ValidateProviderConfigRequest) ValidateProviderConfigResponse\n    ValidateResourceConfig(ValidateResourceConfigRequest) ValidateResourceConfigResponse\n    ConfigureProvider(ConfigureProviderRequest) ConfigureProviderResponse\n    Stop() error\n    ReadResource(ReadResourceRequest) ReadResourceResponse\n    PlanResourceChange(PlanResourceChangeRequest) PlanResourceChangeResponse\n    ApplyResourceChange(ApplyResourceChangeRequest) ApplyResourceChangeResponse\n    ImportResourceState(ImportResourceStateRequest) ImportResourceStateResponse\n    ReadDataSource(ReadDataSourceRequest) ReadDataSourceResponse\n    OpenEphemeralResource(...) OpenEphemeralResourceResponse\n    RenewEphemeralResource(...) RenewEphemeralResourceResponse\n    CloseEphemeralResource(...) CloseEphemeralResourceResponse\n    // ... and others\n}\n```\n\nThe key resource lifecycle operations called during plan and apply:\n\n- **`ReadResource`**: Called during plan's refresh phase. Fetches the current real-world state of an existing resource instance.\n- **`PlanResourceChange`**: Called during plan. Given the prior state and the proposed new state from config, the provider returns the final planned state (possibly with computed unknown values).\n- **`ApplyResourceChange`**: Called during apply. Receives the planned changes and performs the actual API calls to create/update/delete the resource, returning the final real state.\n\n### Provider Plugin Architecture\n\nProviders run as separate OS processes and communicate with Terraform Core over gRPC, using the `tfplugin6` (Plugin Protocol v6) or `tfplugin5` (v5) protobuf-based protocol. Terraform Core has wrapper types (`grpcwrap`, `plugin`, `plugin6`) that implement `providers.Interface` by making gRPC calls to the provider binary.\n\n### Provider Initialization and Management\n\n**`contextPlugins`** (aliased from `loadschemas.Plugins`, `internal/terraform/context_plugins.go`): Holds the provider and provisioner _factories_ \u2014 functions that, when called, start a provider process and return a `providers.Interface`. This is the plugin registry passed into `NewContext`.\n\n**`BuiltinEvalContext`** manages the per-walk provider cache (`providerCache`). When a node needs a provider, it calls the eval context's `InitProvider` method, which:\n1. Checks the `providerCache` map (keyed by provider address string).\n2. If not cached, calls the factory from `contextPlugins` to start the provider process.\n3. Calls `ConfigureProvider` with the evaluated provider configuration block.\n4. Stores the initialized `providers.Interface` in the cache.\n\nThe provider cache is shared across all concurrent graph node evaluations, protected by `providerLock`. This ensures each provider process is started and configured at most once per graph walk.\n\n**`NodeApplyableProvider`** is the graph node responsible for initializing a provider. It runs before any resource node that depends on it, evaluating the `provider {}` configuration block and calling `ConfigureProvider`.\n\n**Stop propagation**: When `Context.Stop()` is called (e.g., on SIGINT), `watchStop` goroutine iterates over all cached providers and calls `p.Stop()` on each, requesting graceful termination.\n\n### Provider Configuration and Instance Management\n\nEach distinct provider configuration block in the Terraform configuration becomes a separate provider instance. The graph uses `CloseProviderTransformer` to add `NodeDestroyableProvider` (close) nodes that are connected downstream from the last resource using each provider, ensuring provider processes are shut down cleanly after their resources are done.\n\n---\n\n## 3. State Management\n\n### State Data Structures\n\n**`states.State`** (`internal/states/state.go`): The top-level state object. Contains a map of `Module` objects (keyed by module instance address), each of which contains maps of `Resource` and `OutputValue` objects. Resources contain maps of `ResourceInstance` objects (keyed by instance key), and each instance holds one `current` object plus zero or more `deposed` objects.\n\n**`states.ResourceInstanceObject`**: Holds the serialized attribute values (as `cty.Value`), the status (`tainted`, `ready`), schema version, and private provider data for a single resource instance.\n\n### Concurrent State Access During Graph Walk\n\nThe graph walker works concurrently (nodes are executed in parallel up to the configured parallelism limit). Safe concurrent state access is provided by **`states.SyncState`** (`internal/states/sync.go`), a wrapper around `State` with a `sync.RWMutex`:\n\n- Read operations acquire a read lock.\n- Write operations acquire a write lock via `beginWrite()`.\n\nThe `ContextGraphWalker` holds three separate `SyncState` instances for different phases:\n\n| Field | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `State` | The \"working\" state being built up during the walk |\n| `RefreshState` | Captures the refreshed (real-world) state during plan |\n| `PrevRunState` | The state as it was at the end of the previous run |\n\nDuring plan, `PrevRunState` tracks the pre-refresh state, while `RefreshState` captures the post-refresh state. Both are deep copies of the input state, ensuring the caller's state object is never mutated.\n\n### State Snapshots for Concurrent Evaluation\n\nWhen `graphWalker` initializes (in `context_walk.go`), it creates deep copies of the input state for each `SyncState`:\n\n```go\nstate = inputState.DeepCopy().SyncWrapper()\nrefreshState = inputState.DeepCopy().SyncWrapper()\nprevRunState = inputState.DeepCopy().SyncWrapper()\n```\n\nThis isolation means that concurrent node evaluations read from a consistent snapshot while writing their results. Node evaluations use `ctx.State()` to access their scoped `SyncState`.\n\n### State Locking and Remote State Backends\n\nState locking is handled at the backend layer, outside the graph walk, by the `statemgr.Locker` interface (`internal/states/statemgr/lock.go`). The `statemgr.Full` interface (`internal/states/statemgr/statemgr.go`) composes `Transient` (in-memory), `Persistent` (disk/remote), and `Locker` interfaces.\n\nRemote backends (S3, GCS, Consul, etc.) implement `statemgr.Full`. The lock is typically acquired before plan/apply starts (in the command layer) and released after completion, regardless of errors.\n\nState is persisted (via `Persistent.PersistState`) during apply after each group of resource changes, rather than only at the end, so partial apply results are recorded. The command layer wraps the state manager and calls persistence after the walk completes.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Execution Flow and Hook System\n\n### Overall Execution Flow\n\nThe entry point for plan is `Context.PlanAndEval` (`internal/terraform/context_plan.go`) and for apply is `Context.ApplyAndEval` (`internal/terraform/context_apply.go`). Both follow the same pattern:\n\n**Plan flow (`planWalk`)**:\n1. Acquire run lock (`acquireRun(\"plan\")`).\n2. Validate config/state dependencies.\n3. Pre-plan: find and apply move statements (`prePlanFindAndApplyMoves`).\n4. Build the plan graph (`planGraph` \u2192 `PlanGraphBuilder.Build`).\n5. Initialize `graphWalkOpts` with a new `plans.Changes` object.\n6. Execute `c.walk(graph, walkOp, opts)` \u2014 the main graph traversal.\n7. Post-plan: validate moves, detect drift, encode changes.\n8. Assemble and return the `plans.Plan` object.\n\n**Apply flow**:\n1. Acquire run lock (`acquireRun(\"apply\")`).\n2. Validate the plan is applyable (not errored, not non-applyable).\n3. Build the apply graph (`applyGraph` \u2192 `ApplyGraphBuilder.Build`).\n4. Decode the plan's `ChangesSrc` using provider schemas.\n5. Execute `c.walk(graph, walkOp, opts)` \u2014 the main graph traversal.\n6. Record check results, prune husks, return new state.\n\n### The Walker Pattern for Graph Traversal\n\n**`Graph.Walk(walker)`** (`internal/terraform/graph.go`): Calls `dag.AcyclicGraph.Walk(walkFn)`, which performs a topological traversal of the DAG with full parallelism. The underlying walk visits nodes only after all their dependencies have been visited, using goroutines.\n\nThe `walkFn` closure for each node:\n1. Determines the node's module scope (`GraphNodeModuleInstance`, `GraphNodePartialExpandedModule`, or global).\n2. Calls `walker.enterScope(scope)` to obtain the appropriate `EvalContext`.\n3. If the node implements `GraphNodeExecutable`, calls `walker.Execute(ctx, node)`.\n4. If the node implements `GraphNodeDynamicExpandable`, calls `node.DynamicExpand(ctx)` and recursively walks the returned sub-graph.\n\n**`ContextGraphWalker`** (`internal/terraform/graph_walk_context.go`): The main `GraphWalker` implementation. Its `Execute` method:\n1. Acquires the parallelism semaphore (`parallelSem.Acquire()`).\n2. Calls `node.Execute(ctx, operation)`.\n3. Releases the semaphore.\n\nThe semaphore (default parallelism: 10) limits concurrent API calls to providers, guarding against rate-limiting.\n\n### The `EvalContext` Interface\n\n`EvalContext` (`internal/terraform/eval_context.go`) provides the evaluation environment for graph nodes. The concrete implementation is `BuiltinEvalContext` (`internal/terraform/eval_context_builtin.go`), which holds references to all shared walker state:\n\n- `State` / `RefreshState` / `PrevRunState` \u2014 concurrent state access\n- `Changes` \u2014 accumulates planned/applied changes\n- `Hooks` \u2014 the list of hooks to call\n- `InstanceExpander` \u2014 tracks module/resource expansion\n- `Deferrals` \u2014 tracks deferred resource actions\n- `EphemeralResources` \u2014 manages ephemeral resource lifetimes\n- `NamedValues` \u2014 caches evaluated variables, locals, outputs\n- `Plugins` \u2014 access to provider/provisioner factories\n\nEach module scope gets its own `BuiltinEvalContext` instance (shared via the `contexts` map), scoped to the module instance address. The `Evaluator` inside each context handles expression evaluation relative to that scope.\n\n### Dynamic Expansion for count/for_each Resources\n\nResources with `count` or `for_each` are handled through a two-phase expansion:\n\n1. **Static graph phase**: The graph contains an _expand node_ (e.g., `nodeExpandPlannableResource`). This node is `GraphNodeExecutable` (to record that the resource exists) and also `GraphNodeDynamicExpandable`.\n\n2. **Dynamic expansion**: When the walker visits an expand node, it calls `DynamicExpand(ctx)`, which:\n   - Evaluates the `count` or `for_each` expression to determine the set of instance keys.\n   - Registers the instances with `InstanceExpander`.\n   - Builds a new sub-graph containing one node per instance (e.g., `NodePlannableResourceInstance`).\n   - Returns the sub-graph.\n\n3. The walker then recursively walks the sub-graph with `g.walk(walker)`.\n\nModule calls with `count` / `for_each` use the same pattern via `nodeExpandModule` and `ModuleExpansionTransformer`.\n\n### Node Execution During Plan vs. Apply\n\n**During plan** (`NodePlannableResourceInstance.Execute`):\n1. Dispatch on resource mode (managed, data, ephemeral, list).\n2. For managed resources (`managedResourceExecute`):\n   a. If not skipping refresh: call `provider.ReadResource` to get current state \u2192 store in `RefreshState`.\n   b. Compute proposed new state from config.\n   c. Call `provider.PlanResourceChange(prior, proposed)` \u2192 get planned new state.\n   d. Record the `ResourceInstanceChange` in `Changes`.\n3. Fire `PreDiff` and `PostDiff` hooks.\n\n**During apply** (`NodeApplyableResourceInstance.Execute`):\n1. Retrieve the planned change from `Changes`.\n2. Fire `PreApply` hook.\n3. Call `provider.ApplyResourceChange(plannedChange)` \u2192 get actual new state.\n4. Record result in `State`.\n5. Fire `PostApply` hook.\n6. Call `PostStateUpdate` hook.\n\n### The Hook System\n\nHooks (`internal/terraform/hook.go`) are the primary extension point for observing Terraform's execution. The `Hook` interface is extensive:\n\n```go\ntype Hook interface {\n    PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, newState cty.Value, err error) (HookAction, error)\n    PreDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState, proposedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PreRefresh(...) (HookAction, error)\n    PostRefresh(...) (HookAction, error)\n    PreProvisionInstance(...) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstance(...) (HookAction, error)\n    PreProvisionInstanceStep(...) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstanceStep(...) (HookAction, error)\n    ProvisionOutput(...)\n    PostStateUpdate(new *states.State) (HookAction, error)\n    Stopping()\n    // import, ephemeral, action hooks...\n}\n```\n\nHooks return a `HookAction` (`HookActionContinue` or `HookActionHalt`). `HookActionHalt` cancels the current operation. The `NilHook` struct provides no-op implementations of all methods, so callers can embed it and override only specific hooks.\n\n**Built-in hooks**:\n- `stopHook`: Registered automatically by `NewContext`. Implements the stop/interrupt mechanism. When `Context.Stop()` is called, `stopHook` is tripped, and subsequent `HookActionHalt` return values unwind the graph walk.\n- `updateStateHook`: Called via `PostStateUpdate` to persist intermediate state to the state manager during apply.\n\n**User-supplied hooks** are passed as `ContextOpts.Hooks` to `NewContext` and prepended to the hook list. The UI layer (e.g., the CLI) uses hooks to display progress output (`PreApply` / `PostApply` display \"Creating...\", \"Creation complete\" etc.).\n\n### Error Handling and Propagation\n\nErrors in Terraform use `tfdiags.Diagnostics` \u2014 a collection of `Diagnostic` objects that can carry warnings or errors, along with source location information.\n\n- Each graph node's `Execute` method returns `tfdiags.Diagnostics`.\n- The walker aggregates diagnostics from all nodes.\n- Non-fatal errors (warnings) are collected in `walker.NonFatalDiagnostics`.\n- Fatal errors halt the walk for that node's subtree (dependent nodes are not visited).\n- The graph walk itself (via `dag.AcyclicGraph.Walk`) continues visiting independent nodes even when one fails, enabling partial plans and partial applies.\n\nAfter a walk, the caller inspects `walker.NonFatalDiagnostics` and `walkDiags` separately, allowing warning-level issues to be surfaced without stopping execution.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Key Extension Points\n\n| Extension Point | Mechanism | Use Case |\n|---|---|---|\n| Provider plugins | Implement `providers.Interface` via gRPC | New resource types, data sources |\n| Hooks | Implement `Hook` interface, pass via `ContextOpts.Hooks` | UI progress, logging, policy enforcement |\n| State backends | Implement `statemgr.Full` | Remote state storage, locking |\n| Graph transformers | Implement `GraphTransformer`, injected into builder Steps | Custom dependency rules, node injection |\n| Concrete node factories | `ConcreteProvider`, `ConcreteResource`, etc. in graph builders | Customizing node behavior per operation |\n| Provisioners | Implement `provisioners.Interface` | Post-creation configuration (legacy) |\n| Overrides (testing) | `mocking.Overrides` passed via `graphWalkOpts` | Mock providers/resources in tests |\n\n---\n\n## 6. Data Flow Summary\n\n### Plan Data Flow\n\n```\nconfigs.Config + states.State\n        \u2502\n        \u25bc\nPlanGraphBuilder.Build()\n  \u251c\u2500 ConfigTransformer     \u2192 resource nodes from config\n  \u251c\u2500 StateTransformer      \u2192 orphan nodes from state\n  \u251c\u2500 ReferenceTransformer  \u2192 dependency edges from config refs\n  \u251c\u2500 transformProviders    \u2192 provider nodes + edges\n  \u2514\u2500 (other transformers)\n        \u2502\n        \u25bc\nGraph.Walk(ContextGraphWalker)\n  \u251c\u2500 nodeExpandModule.DynamicExpand \u2192 per-instance sub-graphs\n  \u251c\u2500 NodeApplyableProvider.Execute  \u2192 provider.ConfigureProvider()\n  \u2514\u2500 NodePlannableResourceInstance.Execute\n       \u251c\u2500 provider.ReadResource()       \u2192 refreshed state\n       \u2514\u2500 provider.PlanResourceChange() \u2192 planned change\n              \u2502\n              \u25bc\n        plans.Changes (accumulated)\n              \u2502\n              \u25bc\n        plans.Plan (returned to caller)\n```\n\n### Apply Data Flow\n\n```\nplans.Plan + configs.Config\n        \u2502\n        \u25bc\nApplyGraphBuilder.Build()\n  \u251c\u2500 DiffTransformer      \u2192 per-instance nodes from planned changes\n  \u251c\u2500 ConfigTransformer    \u2192 whole-resource metadata nodes\n  \u251c\u2500 ReferenceTransformer \u2192 dependency edges\n  \u2514\u2500 (other transformers)\n        \u2502\n        \u25bc\nGraph.Walk(ContextGraphWalker)\n  \u251c\u2500 NodeApplyableProvider.Execute       \u2192 provider.ConfigureProvider()\n  \u2514\u2500 NodeApplyableResourceInstance.Execute\n       \u2514\u2500 provider.ApplyResourceChange() \u2192 actual resource mutation\n              \u2502\n              \u25bc\n        states.SyncState (accumulated)\n              \u2502\n              \u25bc\n        states.State (returned as new state)\n```\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"
}
